Question 0:
You are a linguist specializing in Kalamang. You are given a sentence along with its morpheme breakdown, gloss, and translation. Words are separated by spaces, and morphemes are separated by hyphens. However, a word and its gloss are missing and represented by an underscore. Based on your understanding, please choose the most appropriate option. 
Sentence (with missing item): [...] ins duvrava ___ a tgarnpiartg.
Gloss (with missing item): … GNR need.IMPF.3SG ___ and bacon.M.SG
The English translation of this sentence is:`[...] one needed also cheese and bacon.'
Here is a relevant knowledge point for this example, with the related morphemes and glosses masked: Bare nouns or \isi{noun phrases}, in the sense of noun phrases without determiners, obligatorily occur with mass nouns and in indefinite plural \isi{object noun phrases}. Bare nouns are very frequent in prepositional phrases, mostly with a \isi{locative} meaning (see \sectref{sec:4.2.3}. Example (\ref{ex:baremass}) illustrates mass nouns, (\ref{ex:bareindefpl}) an indefinite plural object \isi{noun phrase}, and (\ref{ex:barepp1}) a \isi{locative prepositional phrase}.
A: word: magnùc	 gloss: cheese.M.SG
B: word: dumagnè	 gloss: cope.INF
C: word: vaschala	 gloss: dishes.F.SG
D: word: téc	 gloss: bit
Please only return the letter (A–D).

Question 21:
You are a linguist specializing in Kalamang. You are given a sentence along with its morpheme breakdown, gloss, and translation. Words are separated by spaces, and morphemes are separated by hyphens. However, a word and its gloss are missing and represented by an underscore. Based on your understanding, please choose the most appropriate option.

The English translation of this sentence is:`[…] that no smith in the whole world would be able to make [things] like him.'

Question 25:
You are a linguist specializing in Kalamang. You are given a sentence along with its morpheme breakdown, gloss, and translation. Words are separated by spaces, and morphemes are separated by hyphens. However, a word and its gloss are missing and represented by an underscore. Based on your understanding, please choose the most appropriate option. 
Sentence (with missing item): A grad ajnta ___ Pardatsch èran nus quátar, tschun buéts.
Gloss (with missing item): and precisely in ___ PN COP.IMPF.1PL 1PL four five boy.M.PL
The English translation of this sentence is:`And precisely in Pardatsch we were four, five boys.'
Here is a relevant knowledge point for this example, with the related morphemes and glosses masked: In the \isi{demonstrative} paradigms, there is one \isi{syncretism}: the masculine singular \isi{determiner}\footnote{Quaj is also used as a form that may determine place names (see example (\ref{ex:dem.unm.pln}) in this section), but this is not the case for the other three demonstratives.} and the \isi{pronoun} which is \isi{unmarked} for \isi{gender} have the same form: the morpheme ___, gljèz, and tschaj.\footnote{There is no such \isi{syncretism} in the quèst-series since in this paradigm there are no pronouns.} This parallels the \isi{syncretism} in the domain of the \isi{adjective}: the masculine singular \isi{attributive adjective} has the same form as the \isi{predicative} \isi{adjective} whose \isi{antecedent} has no \isi{gender} (see \sectref{sec:3.3.1}).
A: word: quaj	 gloss: DEM.UNM
B: word: cunquaj	 gloss: since
C: word: quajnassé	 gloss: DEM.UNM.in_up
D: word: car	 gloss: dear.M.SG.UNM
Please only return the letter (A–D).

Question 47:
You are a linguist specializing in Kalamang. You are given a sentence along with its morpheme breakdown, gloss, and translation. Words are separated by spaces, and morphemes are separated by hyphens. However, a word and its gloss are missing and represented by an underscore. Based on your understanding, please choose the most appropriate option. 
Sentence (with missing item): ___ fò ajn cuṣchina a tschèla fò sé als létgs.
Gloss (with missing item): ___ do.PRS.3SG in kitchen.F.SG and DEM.F.SG make.PRS.3SG up DEF.M.PL bed.PL
The English translation of this sentence is:`One works in the kitchen and the other makes beds.'
Here is a relevant knowledge point for this example, with the related morphemes and glosses masked: The tschèl-series is usually used explicitly or implicitly in contrast to the quèl-series or to the \isi{numeral} in/the morpheme ___ `one' and is best translated by `the other' or `that' (\ref{ex:tschela1}--\ref{ex:tschela4}).\footnote{One of the anonymous reviewers suggested that the demonstratives of the tschèl-series could be medial demonstratives, i.e. demonstratives that refer to objects that are located close to the hearer. This hypothesis implies (1) that the Tuatschin demonstratives are tied to the speech act participants, and (2) that Tuatschin possesses three series of demonstratives that relate the indicated object to the position of the speech act participants, like Spanish este (proximal, close to the speaker) vs ese (medial,close to the hearer) and aquel (distal, further away from both). However, as stated above, Tuatschin makes no such distinction, since there is only one series that has a deictic functions (the quèl-series), and if a spatial deictic distinction is made, the adverbs cò `here' (near to speaker and hearer) and lò `there' (further away from speaker and hearer) must be used. Example (\ref{ex:tschela3}) was uttered while I was sitting with my consultant in a restaurant in front of the city hall of Sedrun. In this example, quèla refers to an object located close to speaker and hearer, where as tschèla refers to an object located at the same distance, but further away, from speaker and hearer, but by no means close to the hearer.}\footnote{To use autar `other' instead of tschèl in such constructions is felt to be more \ili{Standard Sursilvan} than Tuatschin by the native speakers I have consulted.}
A: word: ina	 gloss: one.F.SG
B: word: tgéjnina	 gloss: which_one
C: word: nòva	 gloss: new.F.SG
D: word: quaj	 gloss: DEM.UNM
Please only return the letter (A–D).

Here is a relevant knowledge point for this example, with the related morphemes and glosses masked: The \isi{possessive} paradigm shows one case of \isi{syncretism}: the third person \isi{possessive determiners} have the same form whether the possessor is singular or plural. The forms the morpheme ___/sia are used for singular possessed entities (\ref{ex:the morpheme ___1}) and the forms séjs/sias are used for plural possessed entities (\ref{ex:sejs1}). The \ili{Standard Sursilvan} form lur `their' for third person plural masculine and feminine possessors is not used.

Question 182:
You are a linguist specializing in Kalamang. You are given a sentence along with its morpheme breakdown, gloss, and translation. Words are separated by spaces, and morphemes are separated by hyphens. However, a word and its gloss are missing and represented by an underscore. Based on your understanding, please choose the most appropriate option. 
Sentence (with missing item): Ju a schau ___ agl ésch.
Gloss (with missing item): 1SG have.PRS.1SG leave.PTCP.UNM ___ DEF.M.SG door
The English translation of this sentence is:`I left the door open.'
Here is a relevant knowledge point for this example, with the related morphemes and glosses masked: If the \isi{predicative adjective} or \isi{past participle} is left-dislocated in order to topicalise it (\ref{ex:noagr:1}), or if the adjective or the participle forms a semantic unit with the \isi{verb} as in e.g. schá líbar `let free' or vay mal `have pain' (\ref{ex:noagr:2}--\ref{ex:noagr:7}), it does not agree with the noun it modifies and the \isi{unmarked} form of the adjective is used.

The English translation of this sentence is:
Here is a relevant knowledge point for this example, with the related morphemes and glosses masked: The \isi{polite pronoun} is Vus, which triggers the second person plural form in the verb. There is, however, one exception: past participles. Whereas for masculine singular (and plural) referents, the plural form is used (\ref{ex:vus1}), for feminine singular referents, it is the singular form that is used (\ref{ex:vus2}); the plural only refers to plural referents (\ref{ex:vus3}).

B: word: stadas	 gloss: COP.PTCP.F.PL
C: word: staus	 gloss: COP.PTCP.M.SG
D: word: antira	 gloss: whole

Question 232:
You are a linguist specializing in Kalamang. You are given a sentence along with its morpheme breakdown, gloss, and translation. Words are separated by spaces, and morphemes are separated by hyphens. However, a word and its gloss are missing and represented by an underscore. Based on your understanding, please choose the most appropriate option. 
Sentence (with missing item): ___ mèza vaj santju quaj.
Gloss (with missing item): ___ self.1SG.F have.PRS.1SG feel.PTCP.UNM DEM.UNM
The English translation of this sentence is:\glt`I felt this myself.'
Here is a relevant knowledge point for this example, with the related morphemes and glosses masked: The personal pronouns may be modified by the intensive pronouns mèz `myself', etc. The paradigm is as follows: mèz, -a, tèz, -a, sèz, -a, nus sèzs, -as, vus sèzs, -as, sèzs, -as; however, there is a general tendency in Sursilvan varieties to use sèz for all persons, a development which parallels the case of \isi{reflexive} sa- which is used for all persons in all tenses and moods (see \sectref{sec:4.1} and \sectref{sec:5.5.1}). In the corpus, there are only examples for mèz `myself' and sèz `herself, himself'. These may be used attributively (\ref{ex:the morpheme ___meza}) or predicatively \ref{ex:meza}).
A: word: ju	 gloss: 1SG
B: word: pudju	 gloss: can.PTCP.UNM
C: word: «té	 gloss: 2SG
D: word: fatg	 gloss: make.PTCP.UNM
Please only return the letter (A–D).

However, a word and its gloss are missing and represented by an underscore. Based on your understanding, please choose the most appropriate option. 
Sentence (with missing item): […] la damaun èra la crapa gjù ___ la basèlgja stat òz sén quaj prau.
Gloss (with missing item): … DEF.F.SG morning COP.IMPF.3SG DEF.M.SG stone.COLL down ___ DEF.F.SG church stay.PRS.3SG today on DEM.M.SG field
The English translation of this sentence is:`[…] in the morning the stones where down there on the field where the church is located nowadays.'
Here is a relevant knowledge point for this example, with the related morphemes and glosses masked: \isi{Locative relative clauses} are formed with nù (\ref{relloclogans2}), nù tga (\ref{ex:relloc1}), the morpheme ___ (\ref{ex:relloc2} and \ref{ex:relloc3}), the morpheme ___ tga (\ref{ex:relloc4} and \ref{ex:relloc5}), or only with the \isi{relativiser} tga (\ref{ex:relloc6}). Nùca already contains the complementiser ca -- see Standard Survilvan nua che ‘where that’, also realised as nu che -- but in Tuatschín, ca forms an unanalysable unit with nù.
A: word: nùca	 gloss: REL
B: word: bùca	 gloss: mouth
C: word: tgu	 gloss: REL.1SG
D: word: tgaut	 gloss: warm.ADJ.UNM
Please only return the letter (A–D).

Question 263:
You are a linguist specializing in Kalamang. You are given a sentence along with its morpheme breakdown, gloss, and translation. Words are separated by spaces, and morphemes are separated by hyphens. However, a word and its gloss are missing and represented by an underscore. Based on your understanding, please choose the most appropriate option. 
Sentence (with missing item): Nuṣ èssan ṣgulaj l’ amprém’ jèd’ uòn, cun ___ duaṣ ... buébas.
Gloss (with missing item): 1PL be.PRS.1PL fly.PTCP.M.PL DEF.F.SG first time this_year with ___ two.F … girl.PL
The English translation of this sentence is:`We flew for the first time this year, with our two ... daughters.'
Here is a relevant knowledge point for this example, with the related morphemes and glosses masked: Determiners precede adjectives and nouns. The modifying \isi{noun phrases}, \isi{prepositional phrases}, and \isi{relative clauses} follow the \isi{noun}. Adjectives precede or follow the \isi{noun}; intensifiers precede the \isi{adjective}. If combinations of determiners occur, the \isi{demonstrative} precedes the \isi{possessive} which in turn precedes the \isi{numeral}: quèls nòs ufauns `these our children' -- but these combinations are rare. The only combination of determiners occurring in the corpus is a \isi{possessive} with a \isi{numeral} (\ref{ex:possnum}).
A: word: nòssas	 gloss: POSS.1PL.F.PL
B: word: nòssa	 gloss: POSS.1PL.F.SG
C: word: bjèrs	 gloss: many.M.PL
D: word: tgaut	 gloss: warm.ADJ.UNM
Please only return the letter (A–D).

Here is a relevant knowledge point for this example, with the related morphemes and glosses masked: Determiners precede adjectives and nouns. The modifying \isi{noun phrases}, \isi{prepositional phrases}, and \isi{relative clauses} follow the \isi{noun}. Adjectives precede or follow the \isi{noun}; intensifiers precede the \isi{adjective}. If combinations of determiners occur, the \isi{demonstrative} precedes the \isi{possessive} which in turn precedes the \isi{numeral}: quèls nòs ufauns `these our children' -- but these combinations are rare. The only combination of determiners occurring in the corpus is a \isi{possessive} with a \isi{numeral} (\ref{ex:possnum}).
A: word: duaṣ	 gloss: two.F
B: word: duas	 gloss: two.F
C: word: in'	 gloss: one.F
D: word: zacùnda	 gloss: second
Please only return the letter (A–D).
